The speaking section is recorded instead of live, which some students prefer. TOEFL is widely accepted by universities in the USA, Canada, and several other countries. Knowing how to calculate your percentage correctly helps you meet application rules and show your marks with confidence. A clear percentage makes your report card easy for teachers, admission staff, and future employers to read.Why Percentage Calculation MattersMany schools, colleges, and employers across the globe rely on percentage scores to evaluate applicants. Some schools use GPA or letter grades, but percentages are the easiest way to compare results from different boards and places. Showing your percentage helps scholarship teams and employers see your marks quickly without changing them into another grade system.Percentages give everyone a common language. No matter if you studied in a state board, central board, or international school, a percentage means the same thing everywhere. That is why many online applications ask for a percentage even when you already have grades or a GPA.The Basic FormulaCalculating your percentage of marks is a straightforward two-step process:1.&nbsp;Add the marks obtained in all your subjects.2.&nbsp;Divide this total by the maximum possible marks and multiply by 100.Example: English 78, History 90, Geography 85, Economics 79, Political Science 88, Social Studies 75. Total = 495 out of 600.Now apply the formula: (495 Ã· 600) Ã— 100 = 82.5%.This formula works the same way whether you are calculating for three subjects or tenâ€”only the total changes. If your school includes practical exams or internal assessments, add those marks as well before dividing.Examples for Different Levels10th Class: Suppose your board exams include five subjects worth 100 marks each and you secure a total of 420. Your percentage is (420 Ã· 500) Ã— 100 = 84%.Degree Example: If each semester is out of 800 marks and you score 640, your percentage is (640 Ã· 800) Ã— 100 = 80%.Six Subjects: If you take an extra subject, add all six marks and divide by the total possible marks for those subjects.These examples show that the method never changes. Only the numbers change depending on the subjects or the maximum marks.Tips for Accurate CalculationCheck Board Guidelines: Some boards count only the best five subjects, while others include all papers. Always follow your boardâ€™s official guidelines to know whether to count best-of-five subjects.Use Spreadsheets: In Excel or Google Sheets, type a simple formula: =(Obtained / Total)*100. This eliminates manual errors and saves time.Fraction to Percentage: Divide the top number of the fraction by the bottom number, then multiply by 100. For example, 45/60 = 0.75 Ã— 100 = 75%.Round Smartly: Most institutions accept two decimal places. Rounding to the nearest tenth is usually enough.Double-Check Totals: Before dividing, be sure you added the subject marks correctly. A small addition mistake can change the final percentage.Converting Marks for Study AbroadFor students applying abroad, converting percentages to the grading system used in the target country is very important. In the U.S., colleges normally want a 4.0 GPA. In the U.K., colleges give results in classes such as First, Upper Second, or Lower Second. Australia, Germany, Canada, and Singapore each have their own systems as well.Research the specific conversion rules for each country. Many universities publish their own tables or provide online&nbsp;GPA calculators.&nbsp;Presenting an accurate conversion prevents confusion and speeds up the evaluation of your application. A mentor or academic advisor can also check your numbers before you submit them.Why This Skill Helps Beyond SchoolMastering percentage calculations isnâ€™t only for students. Professionals often need to read performance reviews, track business targets, or study sales data. Knowing percentages helps you make good choices, like when you apply for a job, ask for a raise, or look over a monthly budget. Strong percentage skills build confidence in everyday life, from understanding discounts while shopping to checking interest on a loan.Expert Mentoring with InforensInforens offers mentors you can talk to on live video calls to guide your studies. With opportunities in finance, technology, and international organizations like Amazon and Deloitte, Luxembourg attracts skilled workers globally. For Indian nationals planning to stay in Luxembourg for more than three months, obtaining an Authorisation to Stay (ATS) is a crucial first step. This comprehensive guide, based on reliable information from official sources such as the Luxembourg governmentâ€™s immigration portal and the Embassy of Luxembourg in New Delhi, details the ATS process, visa fees, required documents, and steps to secure a residence permit for a Luxembourg work visa for Indians.Why Choose Luxembourg?Luxembourg offers compelling reasons for Indian professionals to consider relocating:Career Opportunities: Home to global companies and EU institutions, Luxembourg provides excellent job prospects in sectors like finance, IT, and consulting.Multilingual Environment: The widespread use of English, alongside French and German, facilitates integration for Indian professionals.High Quality of Life: Luxembourg boasts top-tier healthcare, education, and safety, making it ideal for professionals and their families.Work-Life Balance: Competitive salaries and a focus on employee well-being ensure a balanced lifestyle.This guide focuses on the Luxembourg work visa for Indians, specifically the ATS process for salaried workers, ensuring you have all the tools to navigate the immigration system.Looking for personal guidance on studying in Luxembourg? Connect with an international student from the University of Luxembourg or Luxembourg Business School today!What is Authorisation to Stay (ATS)?The Authorisation to Stay (ATS) is a temporary permit required for third-country nationals, including Indians, who intend to stay in Luxembourg for more than three months for purposes such as work, study, or family reunification. Issued by the General Department of Immigration, depending on the Ministry of Home Affairs, the ATS is valid for 90 days and serves as the initial step toward obtaining a residence permit in Luxembourg, which also functions as a work permit for salaried roles. The ATS ensures that applicants meet Luxembourgâ€™s immigration criteria before entering the country.How to Apply for a Luxembourg ATSIndian nationals must apply for ATS from India through the Embassy of Luxembourg in New Delhi or its designated visa application center, VFS Global. The application is processed by the General Department of Immigration, and incomplete submissions may lead to delays or rejection.Required Documents for Luxembourg ATSThe following required documents must be submitted:Valid Passport: A copy of your passport, valid for at least three months beyond your intended stay.Criminal Record or Affidavit: An extract from your criminal records or an affidavit from your country of residence.Curriculum Vitae (CV): A detailed CV outlining your professional background.Diplomas and Qualifications: Copies of your educational and professional certificates.Employment Contracts: A signed contract compliant with Luxembourg labor law, dated and signed by both you and your employer.ADEM Certificate: An original certificate from the National Employment Agency (ADEM) authorizing your employer to hire a third-country national.Power of Attorney (if applicable): If someone else submits the application on your behalf.Click here to get support to apply for Luxembourg ATS and Visa PackageDocument TranslationAll supporting documents must be in English, French, or German. If they are in another language, such as Hindi or another Indian language, they require translation by a sworn translator. A list of sworn translators is available at mj.gouvernement.lu.Processing TimeThe processing time for an ATS application is up to 4 months. If no response is received within this period, the application is considered denied, and you may need to reapply. Upon approval, the ATS is sent by post, valid for 90 days, during which you must apply for a long-stay visa.Obtaining a Long-Stay VisaAs India is not exempt from visa requirements (see List of countries requiring a visa), Indian nationals must apply for a type D long-stay visa after receiving the ATS. This visa allows you to travel to Luxembourg for your intended purpose, such as work.Types of Luxembourg Work VisaLuxembourg offers several types of Luxembourg work visa, including:Work Visa for Employed Workers: For those with a job offer from a Luxembourg employer, the most common type for Indians.Work Visa for Self-Employed: For entrepreneurs or freelancers starting a business.Work Visa for Highly Skilled Professionals: For individuals with exceptional skills, often fast-tracked.Intra-Corporate Transferees: For employees transferred within a multinational company.For Indians, the work visa for employed workers is the primary type, requiring an ATS and leading to a residence permit.Required Documents for Type D VisaThe following required documents must be submitted:Valid Passport: Valid for at least three months after the visaâ€™s expiry.The ATS document.Two recent passport-sized photos (35-40mm, taken within the last six months).Proof of health insurance covering at least â‚¬30,000 for medical expenses in Luxembourg.Proof of financial stability (e.g., bank statements from the last six months).A cover letter explaining the purpose of your visit and planned activities in Luxembourg.Proof of accommodation (e.g., rental agreement or hotel reservation).Visa FeesThe visa fees for a type D long-stay visa are approximately â‚¬80. Additional service fees may apply when using VFS Global, such as INR 2112 for processing and INR 800 for courier services. Always verify the current fee with the Embassy of Luxembourg in New Delhi or VFS Global.Processing TimeThe processing time is typically 15-45 days, depending on the completeness of your application and additional checks required.Entering Luxembourg and Applying for a Residence PermitOnce you have your type D visa, you can travel to Luxembourg. Within 90 days of arrival, you must complete the following steps to secure your residence permit, which also serves as your work permit for salaried roles:Declaration of ArrivalWithin 3 days of arrival, visit the administration of the commune where you will reside to declare your arrival. You will need:Your valid passport.The ATS document.Proof of accommodation (e.g., rental agreement or utility bill).You will receive a copy of the declaration, which, along with your ATS, acts as a temporary authorization until your residence permit is issued. More details are available at Guichet.lu - Declaration of Arrival.Medical CheckBefore applying for the residence permit, you must undergo a medical examination and tuberculosis screening at an authorized medical center or the Health and Social Welfare League. Details are available at Guichet.lu - Medical Check.Residence Permit ApplicationApply for a residence permit at the General Department of Immigration, either online via MyGuichet.lu or by post. Strategic Job Preparation from the StartWhat were some key strategies you used to land a job after university as an international student? Interview Process InsightsFor data scientist roles, most of my interview processes were similar. First is the resume screening and a coding round like hackerrank to test basic programming and logic skills. Then a call with the HR personnel describing the role and the interview process followed by discussion about the logistics like work hours, location, and in my case, my visa status. After this, there is usually a take home test to build a Machine Learning (ML) model since that is what my job would entail. And then 1-2 interviews with the senior managers of my prospective team to discuss the solution of the take-home coding test and gauge my data science skills, see a culture fit and have time for me to ask questions about the team too. If everything is good, the last call is to share the job offer followed by negotiations. This charming nation offers an exceptional quality of life, economic stability, cultural diversity, and some of the most scenic cityscapes and countryside in the region. For expats, international students, or professionals moving to Luxembourg, life here presents a unique and rewarding experience.One of the most remarkable things about life in Luxembourg is its diversity. Nearly half the population is foreign-born, making it one of the most international countries in Europe.Luxembourg City, the capital, is a hub for EU institutions and global finance, attracting professionals from across the globe. Those who live in Luxembourg City benefit from a vibrant, multicultural lifestyle. The country has three official languages: Luxembourgish, French, and German, but English and Portuguese are also widely spoken. This multilingual environment means that new arrivals can integrate more smoothly than in many other European countries.Safety and quality of life are standout features. Luxembourg City consistently ranks among the safest in the world, and the country as a whole is known for its political stability, efficient governance, and low crime rates.Families benefit from excellent public services, clean air, and generous social welfare. Public transportation is completely free nationwideâ€”something that few European countries can match. It makes commuting or exploring the country convenient and affordable.Financially, Luxembourg offers some of the highest wages in the world. In fact, it boasts the highest GDP per capita globally. The job market is strong, especially in sectors like banking, EU administration, and IT. Workers benefit from high salaries, comprehensive labor protections, and a strong emphasis on work-life balance.That said, the cost of living in Luxembourg is high, particularly when it comes to housing. Real estate prices in Luxembourg City are steep, and itâ€™s common for expats to spend a significant portion of their income on rent. The Student Route: Your Gateway to Studying in the UK For foreign students who want to pursue higher education in the UK, the Student Route acts as an easy immigration pathway. To go through this process, you must have an acceptance letter from a recognized educational institute. This serves as an official invitation for you to enroll in a particular course. &#8226;&nbsp;&nbsp;Applying for a UK student visa requires completing an online form with your personal information, submitting the required paperwork, and verifying that you meet the point requirements. &#8226;&nbsp;&nbsp;The authorities check your application after you submit it to make sure you meet the requirements. &#8226;&nbsp;&nbsp;If all goes according to plan, you are granted permission to study in the UK with the student visa UK. &#8226;&nbsp;&nbsp;You are permitted to remain in the UK with the visa for the duration of your course and a short period beyond. &#8226;&nbsp;&nbsp;You may research or prepare yourself for your next move during this extra time. In most cases, you are permitted to work part-time while studying at your educational institution. &#8226;&nbsp;&nbsp;You can manage to work full-time during breaks. This aids in budgeting and acquiring real-world experience. The Graduate Route: Your Path to Post-Study Work The Graduate Route is for international graduates looking to stay in the UK after graduation. International students are invited to apply to stay in the UK while working or looking for work after graduation through the UK graduate visa, commonly referred to as the PSW visa. After successfully completing an undergraduate or master's degree, international students may apply to stay in the UK for a maximum of two years. Doctorate holders may request to stay for a maximum of three years. For overseas students looking to advance into the UK workforce, this is an incredible opportunity. &#8226;&nbsp;&nbsp;The PSW full form in the UK stands for Post-Study Work visa. It allows graduates to stay in the country and gain professional experience without requiring sponsorship from an employer. This means you are free to work or search for work at any skill level during the period following your graduation. &#8226;&nbsp;&nbsp;You will be able to work as a freelancer in the UK, complete an internship, or obtain work experience. &#8226;&nbsp;&nbsp;There is no cap on the number of international students who can stay in the UK via the PSW visa, nor is there a minimum salary requirement. &#8226;&nbsp;&nbsp;You can also work multiple jobs at any skill level and change jobs at any time during the visa, as you are not restricted to a single job or employer. Whether your goals are to study, work or travel, this detailed guide will help you go ahead with the key components of being an expert visa applicant. Step 1: Identify the Appropriate Visa Type The first and most important step is to research and choose the right kind of visa that suits your requirements. Different visas are available for different purposes, including job, education, travel, and family reunion. A pretty easy way is to Visit the official immigration website of your destination country to explore the available visa options and choose the one that aligns with your plans. Here are some common types of visas: &#8226;&nbsp;&nbsp; Schengen Visa (Europe): Allows short-term travel across multiple European countries in the Schengen Area. &#8226;&nbsp;&nbsp; F-1 Student Visa (USA): Issued to international students enrolling in academic programs. &#8226;&nbsp;&nbsp; Tier 2 Work Visa (UK): For skilled workers with job offers in the UK. &#8226;&nbsp;&nbsp; Working Holiday Visa (Australia, Canada, New Zealand): Allows young travelers to work while exploring the country. &#8226;&nbsp;&nbsp; Spouse/Dependent Visa (Various countries): For family members joining their partners abroad. &#8226;&nbsp;&nbsp; H-1B Work Visa (USA): For highly skilled professionals working in specialized fields. &#8226;&nbsp;&nbsp; Permanent Residency (PR) Visa (Canada, Australia): For individuals planning long-term settlement. Step 2: Review Visa Requirements Once youâ€™ve identified the visa type, carefully review the specific requirements that it entails. These could include proof of financial stability , hotel reservations, travel insurance, and any other supporting documentation applicable to your visa category. Make a list of the required documents and make sure you have enough time to collect them to make your visa application process easier. You must ensure that every item on the Visa Application Checklist is completed and all required documents are gathered to avoid any delays or complications in your application process. Step 3: Complete the Visa Application Form Most countries offer an Online Visa Application process for visas. Find the application on the official immigration website, then carefully fill it out. You will be expected to share information about your background, past travel experiences, and reason for visiting. Take your time to make sure everything matches your supporting documentation and to prevent errors. Step 4: Gather Supporting Documents Getting the required supporting documents for visa is a crucial step in the Visa Application Process. A valid passport, passport-sized pictures, evidence of funds, acceptance letters (for study visas), and any other documents listed in the application requirements are common paperwork. As you collect the documents, cross each one off your list. Step 5: Schedule Biometrics and Appointments Certain Visa Categories like work visa and study visa need biometric information, like photos and fingerprints. Make sure to plan for any necessary biometric appointments and visa interviews. Be punctual and arrive prepared with all required documents to present during these appointments. Step 6: Pay the Visa Fee Most visa applications come with a processing fee. Visit the official website to determine the applicable fee for your Visa Type and make the payment through the specified channels. Keep the payment receipt as it is a mandatory part of your application. Step 7: Submit the Application Once all of your paperwork is in place, follow the guidelines on the official website to submit your visa application. While certain countries support online applications, others could need in-person trips to an embassy or visa facility. Before submitting, make sure you have all required documents included. Step 8: Monitor Your Submission Online tracking services are offered by numerous immigration agencies. To keep track of the progress of your visa application, use the reference number you were given upon submitting your application. This will notify you as to whether your application has been accepted, is pending approval, or requires any additional information. Step 9: Collect your Visa Once approved, pick up your visa by following the instructions given. While certain countries provide electronic visas, others require you to pick up a physical visa at the embassy or another authorized location. Make sure your passport is available for pickup and that you have all the required paperwork. Well done, you've gotten to the point of applying for visas! Now make trip plans and make sure you follow the requirements for your visa. Make sure your visa is in order and familiarize yourself with any entry restrictions before starting on your trip.
